# Video streaming hardware encoding optimization

## Info

**Summary:**

Goal: improve video streaming to reliably hit 1080p60. User’s latest ask: after the new capture change, frametime buildup got bad again; inspect the latest logs and determine where backlog is now.

Key established findings before the latest interruption
- Hardware H.264 encode on Windows MF is fixed and working.
  - Probe command: `cargo run -p callme-egui --example mf_encoder_probe --release --no-default-features`
  - Probe result after async MFT fixes: `MF H.264 encoder ready (... hw=true, async=true)` with roughly `7.8–9ms/frame` encode at 1080p60.
- Green-tinted receive stream was fixed in `callme-egui/src/yuv_convert.rs` by adding proper YUV offsets (`Y +16`, `U/V +128`).
- Earlier logs proved:
  - send-side/network backlog was not the main issue in the “good” run
  - receive-age stayed ~`1ms avg`, `1–2ms max`
  - the earlier ~46–48 fps cap was mainly sender capture (`18–27 ms/capture`) rather than encode
- Discord screensharing in parallel absolutely tanks capture:
  - bad run: sender capture collapsed to `6.7 fps`, `318 ms/capture`
  - receiver matched that collapse exactly
  - frame age still `0–3ms`, decode kept up
  - conclusion: that case was capture starvation/contended screen capture, not network backlog

Important prior code changes already in repo
1) MF hardware encoder / async fixes
- File: `callme-egui/src/win_mf_codec.rs`
- Fixed proper async MFT handling for hardware H.264 encode.
- Probe/example: `callme-egui/examples/mf_encoder_probe.rs`

2) D3D sample metadata fixes
- File: `callme-egui/src/win_mf_d3d.rs`
- Added sample current length, flush, sample duration, etc.

3) Green hue fix
- File: `callme-egui/src/yuv_convert.rs`

4) Capture instrumentation + pacing
- File: `callme-egui/src/screen_capture.rs`
- Logs now report 5-second window stats:
  - `capture pipeline: X fps, Y ms/capture, Z dropped this window, ...`

5) Reliable-stream stale-send mitigation
- File: `callme-egui/src/app.rs`
- If a video send blocks longer than 150ms:
  - reset QUIC video stream
  - reopen stream
  - request keyframe
- Constants:
  - `VIDEO_SEND_LATENCY_BUDGET = 150ms`
  - `VIDEO_STREAM_RESET_CODE = VarInt::from_u32(0x51)`

6) Lowered auto bitrate aggressiveness
- File: `callme/src/video/mod.rs`
- 1080p60 auto bitrate reduced from ~24 Mbps to ~17 Mbps-ish

7) Receiver instrumentation added
- File: `callme/src/video/transport.rs`
  - Added 8-byte sender timestamp header per frame
  - `recv_frame` now returns `(Vec<u8>, u64)`
  - helper: `frame_age_ms(...)`
- File: `callme-egui/src/app.rs`
  - receive-side logs now show fps, KiB/frame, avg/max age
- File: `callme-egui/src/video_decode.rs`
  - decode logs now show fps, ms/frame, KiB/frame, submitted count, dropped count

Checkpoint commit
- Good checkpoint commit before the latest capture work: `9f0b866 Improve video streaming diagnostics and hardware encode`
- `.gitignore` now includes:
  - `/mcps/`
  - `/terminals/`
- A prior bad commit including artifacts was undone; do not use `89be37d`.

Latest uncommitted work after `9f0b866`
- Added a new direct Windows Graphics Capture path to try to avoid zed-scap’s redundant crop/copy path.
- Files modified/untracked:
  - `M Cargo.lock`
  - `M callme-egui/Cargo.toml`
  - `M callme-egui/src/lib.rs`
  - `M callme-egui/src/screen_capture.rs`
  - `?? callme-egui/src/win_capture.rs`
- Dependency added:
  - `windows-capture = "1.4.4"` in `callme-egui/Cargo.toml`
- New module:
  - `callme-egui/src/win_capture.rs`
- Wiring:
  - `screen_capture.rs` prefers `WindowsCapturer::try_new(...)` first
  - falls back to zed-scap with a log message if unavailable
- Intent:
  - zed-scap’s Windows backend always does `buffer_crop(...)`, even for full-display capture
  - direct WGC path tries to skip that
  - conservative behavior: only takes over if the first direct frame already matches target size; otherwise fallback
- Build status:
  - `cargo fmt` ran successfully
  - `cargo check -p callme-egui --no-default-features` passes
  - Same old warnings remain in `win_mf_codec.rs` about `candidate_err`

Relevant file context for capture work
- `callme-egui/src/scap_capture.rs`
  - wraps zed-scap WGC capture
- `callme-egui/src/screen_capture.rs`
  - source selection and pipeline stats
- `callme-egui/src/win_capture.rs`
  - new direct WGC implementation
- Registry findings:
  - zed-scap source is at
    `C:\Users\Noah\.cargo\registry\src\index.crates.io-1949cf8c6b5b557f\zed-scap-0.0.8-zed`
  - zed-scap has `Resolution::Captured`
  - its Windows path appears to always perform crop/copy work
  - `windows-capture` crates present:
    - `windows-capture-1.4.4`
    - `windows-capture-2.0.0`

Latest interrupted execution state
User said frametime buildup got bad again and asked to check logs.

Commands already run:
1) Latest logs list:
- `Get-ChildItem $env:LOCALAPPDATA\callme -Filter '*.log' | Sort-Object LastWriteTime -Descending | Select-Object -First 8 FullName,LastWriteTime,Length`
- Result:
  - `callme-20840.log` — `7/8/2026 9:21:25 PM`, length `0`
  - `callme-8772.log` — `7/8/2026 9:21:25 PM`, length `109`
  - `callme-18728.log` — `7/8/2026 9:08:23 PM`, length `11193`
  - `callme-6568.log` — `7/8/2026 9:08:22 PM`, length `12837`
  - older runs after that

2) Broad grep:
- `rg -n "(direct WGC|zed-scap|screen capture started|MF H\.264 encoder ready|using MF hardware|capture pipeline|encode pipeline|video receive pipeline|video decode pipeline|video send .*exceeded|video send .* took|queue full|dropped|decoded first|decode error|receiving video)" $env:LOCALAPPDATA\callme -S | Select-Object -Last 360`
- Important visible snippet from newest run:
  - `callme-8772.log`
    - `WARN ... video decode error (#5): no decodable frame found in H.264 data`
    - `INFO ... decoded first video frame (1920x1080)`
    - `INFO ... video decode pipeline: 34.7 fps, 14.5 ms/frame, 28.6 KiB/frame, 233 submitted, 0 dropped this window, 0 dropped total`
    - `INFO ... video receive pipeline from ...: 46.7 fps, 26.9 KiB/frame, 1ms avg age, 2ms max age`
    - later another `video decode error (#1): no decodable frame found in H.264 data`
- This already suggests:
  - receive/network is still basically live (age ~1–2 ms)
  - decode thread is only outputting ~34.7 fps while receive is ~46.7 fps
  - no decode queue drops were logged
  - intermittent decode errors are happening again
- Because the grep output was compacted, exact sender-side capture lines for this newest run were not fully inspected yet.
- `callme-20840.log` is empty and `callme-8772.log` tiny/new at 9:21, so those may be an incomplete/current run. The more reliable completed pair is likely:
  - sender: `callme-6568.log`
  - receiver: `callme-18728.log`
  for the 9:08 run.

Immediate next steps for the next LLM
1) Read the specific latest completed sender/receiver logs directly, not broad grep:
- `Get-Content $env:LOCALAPPDATA\callme\callme-6568.log`
- `Get-Content $env:LOCALAPPDATA\callme\callme-18728.log`
- Also inspect the tiny latest pair just in case:
  - `Get-Content $env:LOCALAPPDATA\callme\callme-8772.log`
  - `Get-Content $env:LOCALAPPDATA\callme\callme-20840.log`

2) In those logs, verify:
- whether direct capture activated:
  - look for `direct WGC capture started`
  - or fallback log `direct WGC capture unavailable, trying zed-scap: ...`
- sender:
  - `MF H.264 encoder ready`
  - `using MF hardware (GPU) encoder`
  - `capture pipeline`
  - `encode pipeline`
  - any `video send ... exceeded`
- receiver:
  - `video receive pipeline`
  - `video decode pipeline`
  - `decode error`
  - `decoded first video frame`

3) Most likely next diagnosis based on the partial newest logs:
- receive is still live, so latency buildup is probably not network backlog
- if decode is ~34 fps while receive is ~46 fps and age remains ~1–2 ms, the likely bottleneck has shifted to receiver-side decode/render, especially since it still uses OpenH264 software decode in `callme-egui/src/video_decode.rs`
- next strong candidate improvement is wiring Windows `MfH264Decoder` from `callme-egui/src/win_mf_codec.rs` into `video_decode.rs`

4) If logs show direct WGC did not activate:
- inspect why `WindowsCapturer::try_new` fell back
- the log message should now include the reason
- if it fell back due to initial frame size mismatch, consider whether the conservative guard is blocking the improvement unnecessarily

5) If logs show direct WGC activated but capture is still ~46–48 fps:
- focus on receiver decode/render next, because partial newest logs already show decode fps significantly below receive fps

Other durable context
- The user is sensitive to time spent on software fallback; hardware encode is already fixed, so don’t frame future work around encoder anymore.
- User wanted logs checked directly, not speculation.
- Worktree after latest capture change is dirty with only the direct-WGC files/dependency changes; nothing has been committed after `9f0b866`.

20.5 ms/capture, 0 dropped this window, 1 dropped total (target 60 fps)\nC:\\Users\\Noah\\AppData\\Local\\callme\\callme-8956.log:54:2026-07-08T19:47:49.136912Z  INFO callme_egui::screen_capture: encode pipeline: 46.8 fps, 11.1 ms/frame (target 60 fps)\n",
```
  "exitCode": 0
}
```

## Assistant

Confirmed from sender log: the new direct WGC path did **not** run. It fell back because it produced `3840x2160` while the app asks for `1920x1080`. Then zed-scap capture starts fine at 1080p but eventually blocks hard (`292ms`, `240ms`, then `1795ms/capture`), and receive mirrors that. So the bad buildup is capture blocking/starvation, not encoder/decoder/network.

I’m going to fix the direct WGC path to accept the native 4K frame and downscale/crop to the requested 1080p instead of rejecting it, so we actually test the intended capture path instead of silently falling back.

**Tool Use:** `shell_command`

```json
{
  "command": "Get-Content callme-egui\\src\\win_capture.rs",
  "workdir": "c:\\Users\\Noah\\Desktop\\callme-app",
  "timeout_ms": 10000
}
```

**Tool Use:** `shell_command`

```json

  "command": "Get-Content callme-egui\\src\\screen_capture.rs",
  "workdir": "c:\\Users\\Noah\\Desktop\\callme-app",
  "timeout_ms": 10000
}
```

**Tool Use:** `shell_command`

```json

  "command": "Get-Content callme-egui\\src\\scap_capture.rs",
  "workdir": "c:\\Users\\Noah\\Desktop\\callme-app",
  "timeout_ms": 10000
}
```

```json
  "command": "rg -n \"struct CaptureFrame|VideoFrame|resize|buffer_crop|I420|Bgra\" callme-egui callme -S",
  "workdir": "c:\\Users\\Noah\\Desktop\\callme-app",
  "timeout_ms": 10000
}
```

```
  "output": "//! Direct Windows Graphics Capture path.\r\n//!\r\n//! waiting for first WGC frame: {e}\"));\r\n            }\r\n        };\r\n\r\n        if first.width != target_w || first.height != target_h {\r\n            let _ = control.stop();\r\n );\r\n\r\n        Ok(Self {\r\n            control: Some(control),\r\n            rx,\r\n            pending: Some(first.data),\r\n            width: first.width,\r\n            height: stutter.\r\n        if let Ok(scap) = ScapCapturer::try_new(target_w, target_h, framerate) {\r\n            return Ok(CaptureSource::Scap(scap));\r\n        }\r\n        let (x, y, src_w, src_h) = Err(RecvTimeoutError::Timeout) => continue,\r\n            Err(RecvTimeoutError::Disconnected) => break,\r\n        };\r\n\r\n        while let Ok(newer) = frame_rx.try_recv() {\r\n            bgra =     if encoder.is_media_foundation() {\r\n                    mf_empty_streak += 1;\r\n                    if mf_empty_streak == MF_EMPTY_FALLBACK {\r\n                        warn!(\r\n                            \"MF encoder produced no output for {MF_EMPTY_FALLBACK} frames, switching to OpenH264\"\r\n                        );\r\n                        encoder = FrameEncoder::try_new(&config)?;\r\n                        mf_empty_streak = 0;\r\n                    }\r\n                }\r\n            }\r\n            Ok(encoded) => {\r\n                mf_empty_streak = 0;\r\n                encoded_count += 1;\r\n                if encoded_count == 1 {\r\n                    info!(\"encoded first video frame ({} bytes)\", encoded.len());\r\n                }\r\n                if encoded_tx.send(Arc::new(encoded)).is_err() {\r\n                    if !no_subscriber_logged {\r\n                        warn!(\"encoded frames ready but no video send task is subscribed yet\");\r\n                        no_subscriber_logged = true;\r\n                    }\r\n                } else {\r\n                    no_subscriber_logged = false;\r\n                }\r\n            }\r\n            Err(e) => {\r\n                encode_errors += 1;\r\n                if encode_errors <= 5 || encode_errors % 60 == 0 {\r\n                    warn!(\"video encode error (#{encode_errors}): {e:?}\");\r\n                }\r\n                #[cfg(windows)]\r\n                if encoder.is_media_foundation() && encode_errors >= 5 {\r\n                    warn!(\"switching to OpenH264 after repeated MF encode errors (last: {e:?})\");\r\n                    encoder = FrameEncoder::try_new(&config)?;\r\n                    encode_errors = 0;\r\n                }\r\n            }\r\n        }\r\n        let encode_time = encode_start.elapsed();\r\n        frame_count += 1;\r\n\r\n        let elapsed = loop_start.elapsed();\r\n        let actual_fps = if elapsed.as_secs_f64() > 0.0 {\r\n            frame_count as f64 / elapsed.as_secs_f64()\r\n        } else {\r\n            0.0\r\n        };\r\n\r\n        if last_stats_log.elapsed() >= Duration::from_secs(5) {\r\n            info!(\r\n                \"encode pipeline: {:.1} fps, {:.1} ms/frame (target {} fps)\",\r\n                actual_fps,\r\n                encode_time.as_secs_f64() * 1000.0,\r\n                config.framerate\r\n            );\r\n            last_stats_log = Instant::now();\r\n        }\r\n\r\n        if frame_count % Arc::new(preview_data),\r\n                width: preview_w,\r\n                height: preview_h,\r\n                actual_fps,\r\n                encode_time_ms: encode_time.as_secs_f64() * 1000.0,\r\n            };\r\n            let _ = preview_tx.try_send(update);\r\n        }\r\n    }\r\n    Ok(())\r\n}\r\n\r\nfn make_preview(bgra: &[u8], src_w: u32, src_h: u32) -> (Vec<u8>, u32, }\r\n\r\n    pub fn capture_bgra(&mut self) -> Result<Vec<u8>> {\r\n        if let Some(frame) = self.pending.take() {\r\n            return self.prepare_frame(frame);\r\n        }\r\n\r\n        loop {\r\n            let frame = self\r\n                .rx\r\n                .recv()\r\n                .context(\"direct WGC capture channel closed\")?;\r\n            if frame.width == self.src_w && frame.height == self.src_h {\r\n                return self.prepare_frame(frame);\r\n            }\r\n            warn!(\r\n                \"dropping direct WGC frame with unexpected size {}x{} (expected {}x{})\",\r\n                frame.width, frame.height, self.src_w, self.src_h\r\n            );\r\n        }\r\n    }\r\n\r\n    fn prepare_frame(&mut self, frame: CapturedFrame) -> Result<Vec<u8>> {\r\n        if !self.needs_resize {\r\n            return Ok(frame.data);\r\n        }\r\n\r\n        let src_img = Image::from_vec_u8(frame.width, frame.height, frame.data, PixelType::U8x4)\r\n            .map_err(|e| anyhow!(\"invalid direct WGC frame buffer: {e}\"))?;\r\n        self.resizer\r\n            .resize(&src_img, &mut self.dst, None)\r\n            .map_err(|e| anyhow!(\"direct WGC resize failed: {e}\"))?;\r\n        Ok(self.dst.buffer().to_vec())\r\n    }\r\n}\r\n\r\nimpl Drop for WindowsCapturer {\r\n    fn drop(&mut self) {\r\n        if let Some(control) = self.control.take() {\r\n            let _ = control.stop();\r\n        }\r\n    }\r\n}\r\n\r\n#[derive(Clone)]\r\nstruct CaptureFlags {\r\n    tx: SyncSender<CapturedFrame>,\r\n}\r\n\r\nstruct CaptureHandler {\r\n    tx: SyncSender<CapturedFrame>,\r\n    dropped: u64,\r\n}\r\n\r\nimpl GraphicsCaptureApiHandler for CaptureHandler {\r\n    type Flags = CaptureFlags;\r\n    type Error = Box<dyn std::error::Error + Send + Sync>;\r\n\r\n    fn new(ctx: Context<Self::Flags>) -> Result<Self, Self::Error> {\r\n        Ok(Self {\r\n            tx: ctx.flags.tx,\r\n            dropped: 0,\r\n        })\r\n    }\r\n\r\n    fn on_frame_arrived(\r\n        &mut self,\r\n        frame: &mut Frame,\r\n        _: InternalCaptureControl,\r\n    ) -> Result<(), Self::Error> {\r\n        let width = frame.width();\r\n        let height = frame.height();\r\n        let mut buffer = frame.buffer()?;\r\n        let data = buffer.as_nopadding_buffer()?.to_vec();\r\n        match self.tx.try_send(CapturedFrame {\r\n            width,\r\n            height,\r\n            data,\r\n        }) {\r\n            Ok(()) => {}\r\n            Err(TrySendError::Full(_)) => {\r\n                self.dropped += 1;\r\n                if self.dropped <= 5 || self.dropped % 120 == 0 {\r\n                    warn!(\r\n                        \"direct WGC capture queue full, dropped {} frame(s)\",\r\n                        self.dropped\r\n                    );\r\n                }\r\n            }\r\n            Err(TrySendError::Disconnected(_)) => {}\r\n        }\r\n        Ok(())\r\n    }\r\n\r\n    fn on_closed(&mut self) -> Result<(), Self::Error> {\r\n        Ok(())\r\n    }\r\n}\r\n",
  "exitCode": 0
}
```

## Assistant

I made the direct WGC path no longer reject the `3840x2160` frames; it now accepts the native frame and resizes to the configured `1920x1080`. `cargo check -p callme-egui --no-default-features` passes with only the existing warnings.

One caveat: this is still a CPU resize after capture. If that performs poorly, the next step is to avoid capturing the 4K physical frame in the first place or use a GPU downscale path. I’m checking whether the `windows-capture` crate exposes capture sizing/cropping so we don’t pay that CPU cost.

as_nopadding_buffer(&mut self) -> Result<&mut [u8], Error> {\r\n        if !self.has_padding() {\r\n            return Ok(self.raw_buffer);\r\n        }\r\n\r\n        let multiplyer = match multiplyer) as usize;\r\n        let buffer_address = self.buffer.as_mut_ptr() as isize;\r\n        (0..self.height).into_par_iter().for_each(|y| {\r\n            let index = (y * self.row_pitch) as       let height = self.height;\r\n\r\n        let bytes = ImageEncoder::new(format, self.color_format).encode(\r\n            self.as_nopadding_buffer()?,\r\n            width,\r\n   "exitCode": 0
```
}
```

## Assistant

The `windows-capture` API doesn’t expose an output resolution; it gives the full physical monitor texture and only supports CPU-readable full buffer/crop. So the current practical fix is: use direct WGC to avoid zed-scap’s blocking path, then resize ourselves. For this machine that means `3840x2160 -> 1920x1080`.

I’m leaving the zed-scap fallback in place, but the next run should show `direct WGC capture started ... resize=true` instead of `direct WGC capture unavailable`.

**Tool Use:** `shell_command`

```json
{
  "command": "git diff -- Cargo.toml callme-egui/Cargo.toml callme-egui/src/lib.rs callme-egui/src/screen_capture.rs callme-egui/src/win_capture.rs Cargo.lock --stat; git diff -- callme-egui/src/win_capture.rs callme-egui/src/screen_capture.rs callme-egui/src/lib.rs callme-egui/Cargo.toml",
  "workdir": "c:\\Users\\Noah\\Desktop\\callme-app",
  "timeout_ms": 10000
}
```

## Assistant

### Latest logs point at capture starvation, not latency backlog

I checked the matching sender/receiver logs:

- Sender: direct WGC **did not activate** because it produced `3840x2160` while the app requested `1920x1080`.
- It fell back to zed-scap.
- zed-scap capture then degraded badly:
  - ~46 fps initially
  - then 20 fps
  - then ~4 fps
  - with capture calls reaching `292ms`, `240ms`, and even `1795ms/capture`
- Receiver mirrored the sender FPS collapse, while frame age mostly stayed low (`~1ms`, one late max spike to `111ms`).

So the “frametime buildup” is caused by the sender capture path blocking/starving. It’s not the encoder, decoder, or QUIC backlog in this run.

### Implemented capture fix

I updated the direct Windows Graphics Capture path so it no longer rejects the native physical monitor frame size.

Before:
- Direct WGC saw `3840x2160`
- App expected `1920x1080`
- Direct WGC aborted
- zed-scap fallback ran and eventually tanked

Now:
- Direct WGC accepts native `3840x2160`
- Resizes to configured `1920x1080`
- zed-scap remains only as fallback

Changed:
- Added/updated direct WGC module: [`win_capture.rs`](file:///c:/Users/Noah/Desktop/callme-app/callme-egui/src/win_capture.rs)
- Wired it before zed-scap fallback in [`screen_capture.rs`](file:///c:/Users/Noah/Desktop/callme-app/callme-egui/src/screen_capture.rs)
- Registered module in [`lib.rs`](file:///c:/Users/Noah/Desktop/callme-app/callme-egui/src/lib.rs)
- Added `windows-capture = "1.4.4"` in [`Cargo.toml`](file:///c:/Users/Noah/Desktop/callme-app/callme-egui/Cargo.toml)

### Verification

Ran:

```powershell
cargo fmt
cargo check -p callme-egui --no-default-features
```

`cargo check` passes. Only pre-existing warnings remain.

### What to look for in the next run

The sender log should now say something like:

```text
direct WGC capture started (native 3840x2160 -> 1920x1080, resize=true, cursor=true)
```

If you still see:

```text
direct WGC capture unavailable, trying zed-scap
```

then we know there’s another startup issue. If direct WGC starts but FPS is still bad, the next target is avoiding the CPU resize / CPU readback with a D3D/GPU downscale path.

## Assistant

The latest 1080p60 run is clean enough to diagnose:

- Direct WGC is active: `native 3840x2160 -> 1920x1080, resize=true`
- Encoder is hardware MF and not the cap: encode is ~`9.6–11.9ms`
- Network/receive is not the cap: receiver age is `0–3ms`
- Sender capture is the cap: capture sits at `22–26ms/capture`, which mathematically limits output to ~38–45 fps
- Direct WGC queue is filling/dropping, meaning Windows is delivering frames but our consumer can’t drain/process them fast enough

So the remaining 45 fps ceiling is the capture path doing a 4K CPU readback plus CPU resize down to 1080p before encode. I’m checking the existing D3D/MF code now to see if we can move that scale/convert step onto GPU instead of CPU.

**Tool Use:** `shell_command`

```json
{
  "command": "rg -n \"encode_bgra|BGRA|NV12|D3D|Texture2D|CopyResource|Scale|VideoProcessor|IMF2DBuffer|lock|Lock2D|MFCreateDXGISurfaceBuffer|as_raw_texture|ID3D11\" callme-egui\\src\\win_mf_codec.rs callme-egui\\src\\win_mf_d3d.rs callme-egui\\src\\win_capture.rs -S",
  "workdir": "c:\\Users\\Noah\\Desktop\\callme-app",
  "timeout_ms": 10000
}
```

**Tool Use:** `shell_command`

```json
  "timeout_ms": 10000
```


## Assistant

There’s a second CPU cost too: after capture/resize returns BGRA, the MF hardware encoder path still converts BGRA→NV12 on CPU before uploading to the GPU encoder. At 1080p60 that stack is currently:

```text
WGC 4K frame → CPU readback → CPU resize to 1080p BGRA → CPU BGRA→NV12 → GPU encode
```

That explains why “hardware encode” alone got us stable but not 60. The next real fix is not another bitrate tweak; it’s removing one or both CPU pixel-processing stages.

**Tool Use:** `shell_command`

```json
{
  "command": "rg -n \"struct ResizeOptions|ResizeOptions|Algorithm|FilterType|Nearest|Convolution|default\" C:\\Users\\Noah\\.cargo\\registry\\src\\index.crates.io-1949cf8c6b5b557f\\fast_image_resize-5.1.*\\src -S",
  "workdir": "c:\\Users\\Noah\\Desktop\\callme-app",
  "timeout_ms": 10000
}
```

## User

**Tool Result:** `TU-033m6fFYXfzUgtNbfcwFve`

Use (0.5, 0.5) for\r\n    /// center cropping (e.g. if cropping the width, take 50% off\r\n    /// of the left side, and therefore 50% off the right side).\r\n    /// (0.0, 0.0) will crop from the top left corner (i.e. if\r\n    /// cropping the width, take all the crop off of the right\r\n    /// side, and if cropping the height, take all of it off the\r\n    /// bottom). (1.0, 0.0) will crop from the bottom left\r\n    /// corner, etc. (i.e. if cropping the width, take all the\r\n    /// crop off the left side, and if cropping the height take\r\n    /// none from the top, and therefore all off the bottom).\r\n    pub fn fit_into_destination(&self, centering: Option<(f64, f64)>) -> Self {\r\n        let mut options = *self;\r\n        options.cropping = SrcCropping::FitIntoDestination(centering.unwrap_or((0.5, 0.5)));\r\n        options\r\n    }\r\n\r\n    /// Enable or disable consideration of the alpha channel when resizing.\r\n    pub fn use_alpha(&self, v: bool) -> Self {\r\n        let mut options = *self;\r\n        options.mul_div_alpha = v;\r\n        options\r\n    }\r\n\r\n    fn get_crop_box<P: PixelTrait>(\r\n",
```
  "exitCode": 0
}
```

## Assistant

Found a concrete issue: `fast_image_resize` defaults to `Lanczos3`, a quality-focused filter. That means the live path is doing a high-quality 4K→1080p resize every frame. For screen sharing, that is the wrong default for 60fps.

I’m going to switch the direct WGC resize to a low-latency resize option (`Nearest`, alpha math disabled) as the smallest testable change. If that gets us near 60, great; if quality is too rough, we can try Bilinear/Box next.

**Tool Use:** `apply_patch`

```json
{
  "patchText": "*** Begin Patch\n*** Update File: callme-egui/src/win_capture.rs\n@@\n use anyhow::{anyhow, Context as _, Result};\n use fast_image_resize as fr;\n use fr::images::Image;\n-use fr::{PixelType, Resizer};\n+use fr::{PixelType, ResizeAlg, ResizeOptions, Resizer};\n use tracing::{info, warn};\n use windows_capture::capture::{CaptureControl, Context, GraphicsCaptureApiHandler};\n use windows_capture::frame::Frame;\n use windows_capture::graphics_capture_api::InternalCaptureControl;\n use windows_capture::monitor::Monitor;\n@@\n     needs_resize: bool,\n     resizer: Resizer,\n+    resize_options: ResizeOptions,\n     dst: Image<'static>,\n }\n@@\n             src_h: first.height,\n             pending: Some(first),\n             needs_resize,\n             resizer: Resizer::new(),\n+            resize_options: ResizeOptions::new()\n+                .resize_alg(ResizeAlg::Nearest)\n+                .use_alpha(false),\n             dst: Image::new(target_w, target_h, PixelType::U8x4),\n         })\n     }\n@@\n         let src_img = Image::from_vec_u8(frame.width, frame.height, frame.data, PixelType::U8x4)\n             .map_err(|e| anyhow!(\"invalid direct WGC frame buffer: {e}\"))?;\n         self.resizer\n-            .resize(&src_img, &mut self.dst, None)\n+            .resize(&src_img, &mut self.dst, Some(&self.resize_options))\n             .map_err(|e| anyhow!(\"direct WGC resize failed: {e}\"))?;\n         Ok(self.dst.buffer().to_vec())\n     }\n }\n*** End Patch"
}
```

## Assistant

### Why it’s still capped around 45 fps

The latest 1080p60 sender log shows the remaining bottleneck is **capture/pixel processing**, not encode/network:

- Direct WGC is active:
  - `native 3840x2160 -> 1920x1080, resize=true`
- Hardware encoder is active:
  - `MF H.264 encoder ready (... hw=true, async=true)`
- Network/receiver latency is fine:
  - receive age mostly `0–3ms`
- Sender capture time is too slow:
  - `22–26ms/capture`
  - 60 fps requires `<16.7ms/frame`
- Direct WGC queue fills/drops:
  - Windows is producing frames, but our processing path can’t drain them fast enough.

The path is currently:

```text
WGC 4K frame
  → CPU readback
  → CPU resize 4K→1080p BGRA
  → CPU BGRA→NV12
  → GPU H.264 encode
```

So “hardware encode” is working, but there are still heavy CPU pixel stages before the frame reaches the encoder.

### Applied a low-risk improvement

I found that `fast_image_resize` defaults to `Lanczos3`, a high-quality resize filter. That’s too expensive for real-time 4K→1080p screenshare.

I changed the direct WGC resize path to use:

- `ResizeAlg::Nearest`
- alpha math disabled

This should reduce the 4K→1080p resize cost substantially. It may make scaled video a bit less smooth, but it’s the quickest way to test whether the resize filter is the 45 fps cap.

Validation:

```powershell
cargo fmt
cargo check -p callme-egui --no-default-features
```

`cargo check` passes with only existing warnings.

Please run another 1080p60 test and I’ll check the logs again. If capture is still above `16.7ms`, then the next necessary step is bigger: GPU-side downscale / GPU BGRA→NV12 so we stop doing CPU readback+resize+color conversion.
